The piechart below breaks down the uploaded sequences into 5 distinct categories.</p><p>6,119 sequences (0.0%) failed to pass the QC pipeline. Of the sequences that passed QC, 21,271 sequences (0.1%) contain ribosomal RNA genes. Of the remainder, 5,442,892 sequences (37.4%) contain predicted proteins with known functions and 8,529,295 sequences (58.7%) contain predicted proteins with unknown function. 539,329 (3.7%) of the sequences that passed QC have no rRNA genes or predicted proteins.</p><p>The analysis results shown on this page are computed by MG-RAST. Please note that authors may upload data that they have published their own analysis for, in such cases comparison within the MG-RAST framework can not be done.</p><p><a class='nav_top' target=_blank href='metagenomics.cgi?page=DownloadMetagenome&metagenome=4637819.3'><img src='./Html/mg-download.png' style='width:20px;height:20px;' title='Download 4637819.3'></a>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style='font-variant:small-caps'>download</span> data and annotations<br><a class='nav_top' target=_blank href='metagenomics.cgi?page=Analysis&metagenome=4637819.3'><img src='./Html/analysis.gif' style='width:20px;height:20px;' title='Analyze 4637819.3'></a>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style='font-variant:small-caps'>analyze</span> annotations in detail.<br><a class='nav_top' href='#search_ref'><img src='./Html/lupe.png' style='width:20px;height:20px;' title='Search 4637819.3'></a>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style='font-variant:small-caps'>search</span> through annotations.</p></div><p><span style='padding-left:15px;'><b>Sequence Breakdown</b></span>

Of these 13,140,289 predicted protein features, 4,620,211 (35.2% of features) have been assigned an annotation using at least one of our protein databases (M5NR) and 8,520,078 (64.8% of features) have no significant similarities to the protein database (orfans). 3,498,859 features (75.7% of annotated features) were assigned to functional categories.</p></td><td rowspan='3' style='padding-left:25px;'></td><td rowspan='3'><h3>Analysis Statistics</h3><div class='metagenome_info' style='width: 320px;'><ul style='margin: 0; <h3>DRISEE
<a target=_blank href='http://blog.metagenomics.anl.gov/glossary-of-mg-rast-terms-and-concepts/#drisee' style='font-size:14px;padding-left:5px;'>[?]</a></h3>
<p>Duplicate Read Inferred Sequencing Error Estimation (<a target=_blank href='http://www.ploscompbiol.org/article/info%3Adoi%2F10.1371%2Fjournal.pcbi.1002541'>Keegan et al., PLoS Computational Biology, 2012</a>)</p>
<p>DRISEE could not produce a profile; the sample failed to meet the minimal ADR requirements to calculate an error profile (see Keegan et al. 2012)</p>

  <p>DRISEE is a tool that utilizes artificial duplicate reads (ADRs) to provide a platform independent assessment of sequencing error in metagenomic (or genomic) sequencing data. DRISEE is designed to consider shotgun data. Currently, it is not appropriate for amplicon data.</p>
  <p>Note that DRISEE is designed to examine sequencing error in raw whole genome shotgun sequence data. It assumes that adapter and/or barcode sequences have been removed, but that the sequence data have not been modified in any additional way. (e.g.) Assembly or merging, QC based triage or trimming will both reduce DRISEE's ability to provide an accurate assessment of error by removing error before it is analyzed.</p>

<p>4,620,211 (35.2%) of the predicted protein features could be annotated with similarity to a protein of known function. 3,498,859 (75.7%) of these annotated features could be placed in a functional hierarchy. 21,271 (0.1%) of reads had similarity to ribosomal RNA genes. </p>
<p>The graph below displays the number of features in this dataset that were annotated by the different databases below. These include protein databases, protein databases with functional hierarchy information, and ribosomal RNA databases. The bars representing annotated reads are colored by e-value range. Different databases have different numbers of hits, but can also have different types of annotation data.</p><p><a href='metagenomics.cgi?page=MetagenomeOverview&metagenome=4637819.3&action=chart_export&name=source_hits&file=download.4637819.3.source_hits'>Download chart data</a></p>

  <p>The pie charts below illustrate the distribution of functional categories for  at the highest level supported by these functional hierarchies. Each slice indicates the percentage of reads with predicted protein functions annotated to the category for the given source. An interactive <a hrep='http://sourceforge.net/p/krona/home/krona'>Krona</a> chart of each functional hierarchy is also available<br>Click on a slice or legend to view all sequences annotated with the indicated category in the analysis page.</p>

  google.setOnLoadCallback(drawChart);
  function drawChart() {
    var color = GooglePalette(4);
    var data = new google.visualization.DataTable();
    data.addColumn("string", "Category");
    data.addColumn("number", "Hits");
    data.addRow(["CELLULAR PROCESSES AND SIGNALING", 641770]);
data.addRow(["INFORMATION STORAGE AND PROCESSING", 582416]);
data.addRow(["METABOLISM", 1542803]);
data.addRow(["POORLY CHARACTERIZED", 632121]);
    var chart = new google.visualization.PieChart(document.getElementById("COG_chart_div"));
    chart.draw(data, {width: 450, height: 300, colors: color, chartArea: {left:50,top:0,width:"90%",height:"90%"}});
    google.visualization.events.addListener(chart, 'select', function() {
      var sel = chart.getSelection();
      if (sel.length > 0) {
        var cat = data.getValue(sel[0].row, 0);
        check_download('COG', cat, 'level1', '4637819.3');
      }
    });
  }
</script>

  google.setOnLoadCallback(drawChart);
  function drawChart() {
    var color = GooglePalette(28);
    var data = new google.visualization.DataTable();
    data.addColumn("string", "Category");
    data.addColumn("number", "Hits");
    data.addRow(["Amino Acids and Derivatives", 471884]);
data.addRow(["Carbohydrates", 611544]);
data.addRow(["Cell Division and Cell Cycle", 66820]);
data.addRow(["Cell Wall and Capsule", 179701]);
data.addRow(["Clustering-based subsystems", 808095]);
data.addRow(["Cofactors, Vitamins, Prosthetic Groups, Pigments", 364213]);
data.addRow(["DNA Metabolism", 199304]);
data.addRow(["Dormancy and Sporulation", 11007]);
data.addRow(["Fatty Acids, Lipids, and Isoprenoids", 173738]);
data.addRow(["Iron acquisition and metabolism", 26078]);
data.addRow(["Membrane Transport", 160089]);
data.addRow(["Metabolism of Aromatic Compounds", 104882]);
data.addRow(["Miscellaneous", 434726]);
data.addRow(["Motility and Chemotaxis", 38567]);
data.addRow(["Nitrogen Metabolism", 58469]);
data.addRow(["Nucleosides and Nucleotides", 161052]);
data.addRow(["Phages, Prophages, Transposable elements, Plasmids", 74385]);
data.addRow(["Phosphorus Metabolism", 43408]);
data.addRow(["Photosynthesis", 7972]);
data.addRow(["Potassium metabolism", 15306]);
data.addRow(["Protein Metabolism", 403248]);
data.addRow(["RNA Metabolism", 193509]);
data.addRow(["Regulation and Cell signaling", 78613]);
data.addRow(["Respiration", 185304]);
data.addRow(["Secondary Metabolism", 25188]);
data.addRow(["Stress Response", 133570]);
data.addRow(["Sulfur Metabolism", 67319]);
data.addRow(["Virulence, Disease and Defense", 144442]);
    var chart = new google.visualization.PieChart(document.getElementById("Subsystems_chart_div"));
    chart.draw(data, {width: 450, height: 300, colors: color, chartArea: {left:50,top:0,width:"90%",height:"90%"}});
    google.visualization.events.addListener(chart, 'select', function() {
      var sel = chart.getSelection();
      if (sel.length > 0) {
        var cat = data.getValue(sel[0].row, 0);
        check_download('Subsystems', cat, 'level1', '4637819.3');
      }
    });
  }
</script>

<img src='./Html/clear.gif' onload='draw_histogram_plot("gc_data_qc", "gc_percent_hist_qc", "% gc", "Number of Reads Post QC");'></div><a name='download_ref'></a><h3>Download This Metagenome</h3><p>We provide download capabilities for the submitted sequences, metadata, and all files with results that are produced in the process of MG-RAST analysis on the <a target=_blank href='metagenomics.cgi?page=DownloadMetagenome&metagenome=4637819.3'>download page for this metagenome</a>. This includes fasta files with annotations using the <a target=_blank href='http://blog.metagenomics.anl.gov/glossary-of-mg-rast-terms-and-concepts/#m5nr'>M5NR</a>.</p><p>We also provide access to the blat alignment summaries underlying our sequence analysis work on the <a target=_blank href='metagenomics.cgi?page=DownloadMetagenome&metagenome=4637819.3'>download page</a>.</p><p>Please note: The graphs on this page allow downloading the underlying information as tables. The search results and most of the pie-charts allow selecting the fraction of sequences in an element to work with in the <a target=_blank href='http://blog.metagenomics.anl.gov/glossary-of-mg-rast-terms-and-concepts/#workbench'>workbench</a> feature on the <a target=_blank href='metagenomics.cgi?page=Analysis&metagenome=4637819.3'>analysis page</a>.</p><a name='analyze_ref'></a><h3>Analyze This Metagenome</h3><p>The <a target=_blank href='metagenomics.cgi?page=Analysis&metagenome=4637819.3'>analysis page</a> provides access to analysis and comparative tools including tables, bar charts, trees, principle coordinate analysis, heatmaps and various exports (including FASTA and QIIME). The <a target=_blank href='http://blog.metagenomics.anl.gov/glossary-of-mg-rast-terms-and-concepts/#workbench'>workbench</a> feature allows sub-selections of data to be used e.g. select all E. coli reads and then display the functional categories present just in E. coli reads across multiple data sets.</p><a name='search_ref'></a>
